Memorial of the Premier's Ordeal 56

The Nanjing Central Party Headquarters held a memorial meeting on the morning of the 11th at 9:00 AM to commemorate the Premier's ordeal in London. Chiang Kai-shek, Ding Weifen, Shao Yuanchong, Chen Bulei, Zhou Qigang, Wang Boqun, Miao Peicheng, Chen Lifu, Chen Zhaoying, Zhang Daofan, and approximately 600 other staff and guests attended. Chairman Ding Weifen and Shao Yuanchong reported, roughly saying that the Premier escaped to Japan and the United States, and then to the British capital, because the first uprising in Guangzhou had failed. The Manchu government tricked the Premier into the Chinese embassy in London. The Premier remained unyielding and was later released with the help of British friends. In the Premier's life, this was just one of many difficulties and failures. Whenever the Premier encountered difficulties, he always held on to a consistent spirit. The more difficult it was, the more his courage increased. In the current national crisis, this can be an encouragement to our spirit. If a nation is aware of the oppression of the environment, it must be determined to break the difficulties of the environment before it can save itself. When the Premier was in Guangzhou, he was oppressed by more than 30 foreign ships, but he never changed his position on recovering the customs. The Premier, as a single person, living in a corner, was not subdued by external forces. Now we bear the responsibility of the entire country. If we can maintain the principle of national self-determination, any difficulties cannot be avoided. This national crisis is to test whether we have the ability and qualifications for independence. The right to national survival must be controlled by ourselves, not by others. The Premier relied entirely on his own strength for his revolutionary life. Building a revolutionary cause never vainly hoped for success or sought unexpected things. The current crisis is to test whether we are qualified to survive. If we have the power to save ourselves, we can talk about national self-determination. Otherwise, if any foreigners come to oppress us, we will inevitably be naturally eliminated. Today's commemoration allows us to recognize the Premier's responsibility to revive the nation. Now, because of this national crisis, we should use the great teachings to cultivate our personality as a standard for our work. Only in this way can any difficulties prevent us from surviving. After Shao's report, the ceremony was completed and the meeting was adjourned. (November 11th Central News Agency)

The Nanjing Municipal Party Department convened representatives from party departments at all levels, agencies, organizations, and schools on the morning of the 11th to hold a commemoration of the 35th anniversary of the Premier's ordeal in London, with more than 300 representatives attending. (October 10th Central News Agency)

The Beiping Municipal Party Department held a commemoration of the 35th anniversary of the Premier's ordeal this morning, with more than 200 representatives from all walks of life attending. Chairman Zhou Dawen and Chen Shiquan reported that the petition groups from various counties and cities in Hebei Province against the production and sales tax have been canceled with the approval of Vice Zhang. They thanked all sectors for their assistance and sent letters to all sectors to express their gratitude. (November 11th Telegram)

(3) Wang Jiazeng was appointed as the commander of the newly compiled 3rd Division of Gansu Province, and Huining and other counties were designated as defense areas. (November 11th Special Dispatch)

Important Foreign Telegrams 78

The New German Cabinet Established Amidst Storms

Prime Minister Brüning Also Serves as Minister of Foreign Affairs

Future Fate Depends on the Nationalist Party

Berlin, 9th, National Society Telegraph - Brüning's second cabinet was announced tonight amidst storms. However, judging from the current situation, its fate is precarious. Even Brüning himself knows that he will not last long in office. Therefore, the ministers of both the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the Ministry of Interior have not yet been formally appointed. Foreign affairs are the most important task at present, and at this time of national difficulty, internal affairs are even more indispensable. It is now planned that the former Minister of Defense, Groener, will take charge of internal affairs, while Brüning will temporarily take charge of foreign affairs. In Brüning's second cabinet, the only one who can be called a new member is the Minister of Economy, Warmbold. Warmbold was previously the director of the dye trust's agricultural department and is truly an economic expert rather than a politician. The Minister of Transportation, Treviranus, is also a member of Brüning's cabinet. Gürtner has been appointed Minister of Justice and is a permanent secretary in the cabinet's Justice Department, also a non-partisan figure. The others, such as the Minister of Finance, Dietrich, and the Minister of Posts, Schäffer, all remain in their old positions. Brüning is now showing signs of exhaustion, having been running around for 48 hours nonstop. However, the fate of Brüning's cabinet depends on the hands of the Nationalist Party. If the Nationalist Party insists on joining the opposition, then the fate of the new cabinet will be short-lived. A vote of no confidence will be put forward in parliament next week. Although the Social Democratic Party tends not to vote, it is difficult to avert the crisis. Currently, the German National People's Party is also convening an important military conference in Harzburg, and representatives of the Nationalist Party are also participating in the discussion. The steps the Nationalist Party will take in the future will not be announced until Sunday.

Important News - Japanese Planes Bomb Jinzhou 81

Bombs and Machine Guns Fired for Half an Hour

Extremely Heavy Public and Private Losses Inside and Outside the City

Tianjin Communication: Since Shenyang was captured, the Liaoning Provincial Government was long ago occupied by the Japanese army, and all political power cannot be exercised. The entire Liaoning Province has fallen into a state of anarchy. Zhang Xueliang, because Liaoning Chairman Zang Shiyi is still imprisoned by the Japanese army and has lost his freedom, temporarily appointed Mi Chunlin, director of the Northeast Arsenal, as acting chairman to go to Jinzhou to organize a temporary provincial government. The organization was completed on the 28th of last month, and they worked in the Northeast Jiaotong University school building. At the same time, he issued an order to all counties that all official documents should be sent to the Jin County government for handling. All subordinate departments were also set up in one place. Most of the staff of the provincial government's departments live in the Jiaotong University. Recently, the Japanese have been working hard to promote the independence of Liaoning and Jilin and at the same time want to seize all the political power of the two provinces. They are taking a hostile attitude towards the temporary Liaoning provincial government formed by our side. The day before yesterday (the 7th) in the afternoon, a plane came to Jinzhou and circled in the air for a long time before leaving. Ordinary people already knew that it had malicious intentions and were very worried. Although the Northeast 12th Brigade of Zhang Tingchu was stationed inside and outside the city, because they received orders from their superiors to only sacrifice and not resist, they did not make any preparations. At 1:20 pm yesterday, a large squadron of Japanese planes (reportedly 12 in total) suddenly flew from Yingkou. When passing the Dawa station on the Gouying branch line of the Beining Railway, they dropped a bomb, but fortunately it landed in an open space and there was no loss. At about 2:15 pm, they arrived in Jinzhou and dispersed in the sky above Jinzhou, randomly dropping bombs inside and outside the city and descending to the very bottom, using machine guns to strafe the people who had no resistance or self-defense preparations. Zhang Tingchu's brigade did not fire a single bullet at the Japanese planes because of the principle of non-resistance. The work of the Japanese planes bombing and machine-gunning lasted for more than half an hour. They did not leave until 3:00 pm, feeling satisfied, flying in the original direction. The number of bombs dropped has not been investigated in detail, but it is known that more than 38 have exploded. The damage near the station is extremely heavy, because the target of the Japanese planes was the Liaoning Provincial Government Office in the Northeast Jiaotong University next to the station. Therefore, five or six bombs fell in the station and car barn. A locomotive was destroyed, one passenger car No. 141, and one official car No. 117. Several car barns were also destroyed. More than ten railway workers were injured and six or seven died. The exact number of deaths and injuries in the provincial government has not yet been ascertained, but it is said that a Russian teacher at Jiaotong University was injured by the bombing. The electric wires in front of the railway hospital were all blown off. The residents inside and outside the city showed extreme chaos, carrying things and fleeing. The detailed number of deaths and injuries has not yet been ascertained. It is said that the dead reached 20 or 30, and the injured were 40 or 50. Many houses were also destroyed. The Tiancheng Inn and a certain fruit shop near the station were destroyed by the bombing. Zhang Zuoxiang's private residence - since Zhang came to Jinzhou to attend to his father's illness, he ordered the Beining Road to build a branch line directly to his gate so that his private car could park there. The car was specially prepared by the Jihai Road and was extremely luxurious. Because Jinzhou's business was not developed, it often went to Shanhaiguan to shop. This time, Zhang took the car to Beiping and was not destroyed. However, there were tracks in front of Zhang's residence, which were easily targeted by planes, so a bomb also fell in the residence. The provincial commissioners of the provinces are not always working in the provincial government, so there are no reports of casualties. At the same time, seven Japanese planes were found circling for a long time at the Goubangzi station before leaving. The people of Jinzhou are extremely terrified. Railway workers are in constant danger and have telegraphed the General Administration for instructions. It is also heard that this morning, the Japanese army opened a train of armored cars to Tongliao County, destroying a section of the tracks in the middle of the south station of the county and demolishing the freight yard. Mines were buried nearby, and a Japanese plane scattered leaflets in the air. (October 9th)

Shenyang Under the Iron Heel of the Japanese Army 82

Northeast People's Anti-Japanese Association Receives Beiping Press

Beiping Communication: The Northeast People's Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association held a reception for news reporters from Beiping City at the Fengtian Guild Hall at 2 pm yesterday to report on the organization's process and the Japanese atrocities in Shenyang. Chairman Wang Huaichi delivered an opening speech, reporting on the association's purpose and internal organization. Next, Gao Heiquan, inspector of the Liaoning Education Department, reported on the recent situation in Shenyang, saying that he arrived in Beiping from Shenyang on the 4th. Because he went to the city every day to investigate, he knew more details. Here is a description: (1) Military circles: The arsenal and ordnance factory were occupied by the Japanese army, which is well known. I personally saw 30 or 40 Japanese army trucks going back and forth to transport military supplies to the Japanese station from the upstairs in my residence. There were also trucks transporting miscellaneous items every night, which I thought were items seized. However, they were not transported during the day. The Japanese are very hostile to the military. When I came to Beiping, there were very few plainclothes soldiers on the streets. Because the city police were captured by the Japanese army, there were no traces for two days. After negotiations by the maintenance association, 60 unarmed police officers were stationed. On the 28th, after several negotiations, each district began to distribute three guns, but without bullets. As a result of another negotiation on the 1st, 15 bullets were issued for each gun. (2) Government circles: When I entered the city on the 2nd, I personally saw the Japanese army smashing the door plaques of various agencies. The agencies were all occupied. In the first few days, some people still went to work inside, but the situation became more and more panic-stricken. Now there are not many. However, it is heard that the municipal office, the negotiation office, and the official silver house still have people working. The Education Department was closed on the 1st, and Director Jin (Yufub) was arrested and imprisoned in the Japanese Military Police Headquarters with Chairman Zang. It is rumored that the Japanese ordered him to sign a contract for Sino-Japanese joint church management. If he agrees, he will be released, but there has been no news yet. The principal of the 10th Elementary School was also arrested because the contractor used Japanese kiln bricks when building the building and did not pay the price. He was released after paying 1,600 yuan in foreign currency and making a false receipt. He has now escaped. In addition, the principal of the 2nd Industrial Materials School was also reportedly arrested. (3) Business circles: Three or four days after Shenyang was occupied, there was a rice robbery due to the inconvenience of shopping. I personally saw it once in Xiaonanguan. Later, other goods were also robbed from time to time. After the maintenance association was organized, it was unable to stop it. So far, small shops are only open for business for two hours a day, and large stores dare not do business. (4) Industrial circles: Except for the British and American Tobacco Company and foreign factories, which are still working as usual, Chinese small factories have all stopped working. The spinning mill and arsenal were occupied. The arsenal workers initially went to the station and granary to receive food and could still get one dou of rice, but it gradually decreased, from five sheng to one sheng. I don't know what the situation is now. (5) Transportation: The Shenhai Road is still not open. The South Manchuria Railway is extremely crowded, with many refugees. The Beining Road also operates irregularly. There is no room for passengers on the train. The four streetcars in the city have been opened, and public buses have been extended to Dadongmen, as if it were Japanese territory. (6) News media: The Fengtian Public Newspaper is also published, but it states that it only publishes Japanese news. In addition, there is a Fengtian Public Newspaper, which is obviously run by the Japanese. The New Asia Daily seems to have also surrendered. Newspapers from other ports are smuggled in secretly. The Dagong Newspaper was originally allowed to be sold by the municipal office, but the branch manager was arrested by the Japanese military police for selling it, and the newspaper was completely burned. (7) Finance: Fengpiao is still in circulation. Initially, 80 yuan was equivalent to one yuan in silver, but it later rose slightly to 75 yuan per silver yuan. Jinpiao was initially 2.8 yuan, but later it was also 2.45 yuan. The Sino-Japanese and Communications Banks have opened, and there is also a saying that the official silver house is forced to open. Its business methods are only accepting and not paying. Recently, the Japanese army checked the accounts once and did not allow the payment of deposits from various agencies. Individuals who have not had their deposits confiscated are also not allowed to withdraw them. (8) Order: Because there are not many people in the city, it cannot be said to be chaotic. It can only be said to be "serious panic." Initially, the Japanese artillery drove through the streets to show force, but it gradually decreased. However, the sound of gunfire on the streets every night increased day by day. The panic among the citizens is even worse. There are now two Chinese agencies, the Security Maintenance Association, the Citizens Maintenance Association, and the Self-Defense Police Bureau, but they are of no practical benefit. The police bureau seems to be effective during the day, but it is helpless at night. Recently, there is a pessimistic saying about the local maintenance association. (9) Charity: The Red Swastika Society has now set up five porridge shops to provide relief to refugees. The Japanese army also used trucks to spread dry biscuits stored in the granary on the ground along the streets. People scrambled to eat, but this cannot really be called relief. In addition, there is also the Red Cross that sets out daily to provide relief. (10) Robberies: The merchants and people of Shenyang have recently formed a merchant group, with more than ten people in each group, walking along the street with wooden sticks, but it is actually of no use. Robberies occur frequently, with Beiguan being the worst, Nanguan second, and Xiguan the least. The victims are mostly middle and lower-class families. After the people are caught, they are burned under the neck with paraffin wax to force them to ask for money. Koreans are involved in all major robberies. Even if Japanese soldiers arrive, they will not intervene. The spinning mill was occupied by Koreans, and the 3rd Middle School was robbed. Northeast University also suffered losses, so the people fear the Koreans more than the Japanese. (11) The Japanese army was previously dispersed in various places, but has recently been concentrated in one place. Therefore, from the surface observation, there are not many, but in fact they have not withdrawn. The most troops are stationed outside Ximen. The Japanese station changes defenses every day. There is a branch office of the Japanese Military Police in Huanggu屯, and there are also many Japanese soldiers in Juliu River. (12) The people: The people of Liaoning have been oppressed by the Japanese for a long time and have suffered this unexpected disaster. Therefore, they are working hard in secret, but there is no performance on the surface. Next, Zheng Xiangmao, the head of the Liaoning Branch Rescue Team of the Chinese Red Cross Society, reported on the statistics of deaths and injuries, saying that the losses on the property after the fall of Liaoning have not yet been investigated and counted in detail. The death of his life, according to my own investigation, is considered to be more accurate than any newspaper. Han Yunpeng was killed on the morning of the 19th, and our association provided relief. He died due to serious injuries. At that time, the Japanese army offered rewards for buying the bodies of senior military officers, and there was a robbery of corpses. Later, the family paid a corpse fee of 400 yuan to protect it. According to the investigation and statistics, there were 87 seriously injured people in Beidaying. The Japanese army did not allow rescue and eventually died tragically. It was a tragedy that the world has not seen. In addition, 39 policemen died and 60 were injured, 144 soldiers died and 127 were injured, 167 civilians died and 270 were injured, and 220 workers died and 110 were injured. These were all investigated by our association, and the rest are unknown. After the report, the meeting adjourned. (8th)

One Glimpse of the Japanese Army's Barbarity in Changchun 83

Changchun Communication: After the Japanese army occupied Changchun, its atrocities have been increasing. Now, the recent actions of the Japanese army will be described separately below to inform the people of the country.

Cutting Down Trees and Burying Electric Poles: The Japanese army buried electric poles and installed electric wires in Changchun City. The work was once suspended on the 25th of last month. Unexpectedly, it started again on the 2nd of this month, burying poles and hanging wires along the road, directly to the Nanling camp. It is said that the Japanese side regards Nanling as a fortress and plans to transfer heavy troops to garrison it, using the remaining barracks of our army and adding some barracks, so the buried electric wires are specially for military use. Dajing Road has been buried to the west of the county government's Fourth Road Street Road South, and Dama Road has been buried to the commercial area outside the North Gate. The construction of the third, fourth, and fifth roads has been mostly completed. It has been found that Nanling is about 15 miles from the city. The Japanese commander Duomen has now limited the telecommunications bureau to complete the communication by the 15th of this month. At present, the road protection trees on both sides of the roads in our city have been cut down. On the 28th of last month, Duomen issued a so-called edict, which stated that "the Northeast regime has been overthrown, and you have also lost your support. It is better to obey the power of the Japanese Empire. The troops under the command of Li Zhenshou and other troops should come to surrender their weapons. If you do not come to surrender quickly, our army will carry out a sweeping campaign." The absurdity and barbarity are outrageous.

To Restore Telecommunications, You Must Speak Japanese: The wired and wireless telegraphs in Changchun, as well as the Changchun-Liao-Ha-Hei long-distance telephone, and all communication agencies have been blocked by the Japanese army, who have sent personnel to monitor and guard them, and are not allowed to send reports or communicate, so that internal and external news is cut off and communication is cut off. On the 1st of this month, it was allowed to restore a part of Jilin-Changchun, but although it was allowed to send reports and communicate, it must be checked by the Japanese before it is allowed to be sent and received. All military and political intelligence and news telegrams are still prohibited, and the telegrams are prohibited from using passwords, and the communication must be spoken in Japanese. What is the difference between this kind of restriction and not opening it at all? Now, the regulations of the Japanese army on the revival of communications in Changchun and Jilin are recorded below, and their restrictions and bans can be generally seen: (A) First General Rules: (1) These regulations relate to the regulations on the revival of Chinese communications that have been suspended due to incidents. (2) From now on, communications in Changchun City and Jilin City, as well as communications from Changchun and Jilin to various places, shall be carried out in accordance with these regulations. Military return lines shall not be used for general communications. National wireless telegraphy is temporarily prohibited as it is. (B) Second Implementation Method: One is wired communication. (5) When sending and receiving wired telegraphs, it must be inspected by the Japanese Garrison Commander or other designated person. (6) The Japanese Garrison Commander will send the Chinese Telegraph Bureau for inspection. In Changchun, it will temporarily receive assistance from the telecommunications bureau staff managed by the Kanto Hall. (7) Telegraphs must not be used with passwords. Two are telephones. (8) When communicating by telephone, it shall be carried out in accordance with the following methods: 1. From Changchun and Jilin to various cities, those who want to communicate must temporarily go to the telephone bureau and are only allowed to communicate in Japanese. However, the county public security bureau telephone is allowed to use Chinese, but surveillance officers will be sent to the bureau to monitor. 2. Regarding mutual communication in the city, it shall be allowed according to the progress of communication restoration. (C) (Supplementary Provisions: These regulations shall be implemented from October 1. The above eight restrictive examples are enough to control the mouths of the Chinese people. Whether to restore or not is not important. It is simply that the Chinese have no right to send reports.

Planes Throw Bombs and Kill Farmers: After Changchun fell, five or six Japanese planes flew in the sky to show force every day, no less than ten times. They had not yet thrown bombs to hurt people. Unexpectedly, at 10:25 am on the 2nd of this month, a Japanese plane took off from the Erdao Airport and flew to Nanling. After flying to Nanling at about 11 o'clock, it circled in the air. At that time, there were 50 or 60 poor people, men and women, in the Yuanjia Wobao, East and West Gaotaizi, and Zhujia Datun areas southwest of the city, collecting radishes and cabbage in the Nanling Daying Garden. The plane saw it, lowered its altitude, and flew around the farmers in each village for several circles, attracting people to gather and watch. It actually threw a bomb at the crowd, and with a loud bang, more than 20 people were killed and 15 or 16 injured. After throwing the bomb, the plane flew to the sky in the city. When the bomb exploded, the citizens all suspected that it was a landmine buried by the Japanese army in Nanling, and did not know that it was a plane throwing a bomb. It was not until 8:00 am on the 3rd that the Red Swastika Society reported it and sent personnel to rescue the injured and bury the bodies before they knew the truth. Forty or fifty more of our innocent Chinese people were killed or injured by Japanese planes. The brutality of the Japanese army is increasing and it is also very tragic.

The Japanese Army Goes to the Countryside to Search for and Confiscate Civilian Guns: Duomen, commander of the 2nd Division of the Japanese Army, sent more than 60 infantry soldiers from the 29th Regiment from the Toudaogou Japanese boundary to the towns of Xiaohelong and Wanbaoshan in the 235 districts of the county north of our city, as well as the villages of Sandaogou, Sijianfang, and Liao Jia Youfang, starting at 10:00 am on the 2nd of this month, with two handheld machine guns and one mountain gun. At 8:25 am on the 3rd, Changgu, the commander of the 3rd Brigade, sent five or sixty soldiers from the 4th Regiment from Toudaogou to the areas of Dafangshen, Zhujia Wobao, Qiaojia Wobao, and Fanjiadian in the 9th district of our county, with two mountain guns and two machine guns. At 10:00 am on the 4th, a part of the soldiers from the 2nd and 3rd squadrons, 40 or 50 people, set off from the Japanese boundary to the 6th, 7th, and 8th districts of the county, Sijianfang, Hadawobao, Dahelong, Yujiadian, Wanjiaqiao, and Shaoguodian, with two machine guns and steel guns. What is the intention? At first, few knew. It was not until the afternoon of the 4th that villagers came to the city to report that the Japanese army had been coming to the villages in each district every day since the 2nd of this month, searching for civilian self-defense guns and bullets from house to house, intimidating and coercing them, and being extremely violent. If they were not satisfied, they would beat and scold them. In three days, 150 or 60 civilian guns and 20,000 bullets were confiscated in the villages in the northern part of the city. Wherever the Japanese army passed, the civilian guns were confiscated. Generally, the villagers fled and avoided each other. At present, the bad news of the Japanese army going to the countryside to search for guns has spread throughout the county. Most of those with guns have taken them far away. (4th)

Japanese Conspiracy to Disrupt the Chinese Eastern Railway 84

Supplying White Russian Bandits with Guns and Bullets

Ordering Them to Invade the Dongtie-Haman Line

Su Bingwen Has Sent Troops to Defend

Harbin Communication: White Russian bandits have recently been discovered in the Xiaolingzi and Beidaheshan areas near Hulunbuir on the Dongtie-Haman Line. The leader is a White Russian brigade commander under Zhang Zongchang. His base is in Woniugou, near the Zamiencaimu Company, where he has built a solid fortress with more than 100 horses. The guns and bullets are all new and sufficient, with two machine guns and one small gun. A few days ago, they robbed various small stations near Miand渡河 and planned to destroy the railway line. The background is the Japanese-funded Zamien Caimu Company, which secretly supplies guns, bullets, and food, intending to obstruct the traffic of the Chinese Eastern Railway. The Soviet Union will inevitably send troops to protect the road, and Japan can also send troops to North Manchuria at that time to divide the color with the Soviet Union. Su Bingwen, the commander of the Hulunbuir Garrison, has learned of the plan. On the 1st of this month, he specially sent his aide-de-camp Yan Yongsheng and Chang Tuanfu, an infantry company and a cavalry company from the 6th Infantry Regiment, carrying two mortars and two machine guns, to the mountains to search and suppress the bandits. It is heard that they encountered the bandits at the Naobao Xiaozhan on the morning of the 2nd. After a joint suppression by the cavalry and infantry, more than ten bandits were killed. They are still chasing the bandits. Su is afraid that the bandits will escape into the Zamien Caimu Company and rely on the Japanese as a talisman. He specially telegraphed the provincial capital to ask for a notification to the Japanese consul. On the one hand, he also formed a road patrol team with 300 soldiers, carrying machine guns and mortars, and patrolling back and forth between Hailar and Manzhouli in a train. He also telegraphed Zhang Dianjiu, brigade commander of the 1st Infantry Brigade in Zhalantun, Regiment Commander Zhang of the 2nd Infantry Brigade in Miand渡河, and Regiment Commander Sun of Andada Station, ordering them to send troops to assist in the suppression. The original telegram is as follows: (Telegram 1) The Russian bandits lurking in the Xiaolingzi area are being supplied by the Japanese in the Zamiencaimu Company, which is not only disrupting the local area by destroying the road line, but also the autumn of Liaoji's troubles. The situation in North Manchuria is of great importance. Together with another telegram, it is hoped that the subordinates will be seriously vigilant and send a team to suppress it thoroughly, so as to eliminate the roots. (Telegram 2) According to the report of Regiment Commander Zhang of Miand渡河, dozens of White Russian bandits were found 100 miles north of Xiaolingzi, and it was also heard that the Zamiencaimu Company was supplying the White Russians, trying to disrupt the situation. The regiment was immediately ordered to be responsible for the suppression and dispatched Commander Bao's detachment to assist in the suppression, so as to eliminate the roots. On the one hand, the military department was requested to notify the Japanese Consul Shimizu to avoid misunderstandings when Commander Bao's team went to the forest farm. (October 3)

National Day in the Capital 85

Yesterday (the 10th) was the 20th National Day of the Republic of China, and the National Government specially held a military parade to show its grandness. The location was the Ming Palace Airfield. Yu Youren, Kong Xiangxi, Shao Lizi, Shao Yuanchong, Fang Juehui, Dai Chuanxian, Chen Bulei, Chen Shaokuan, Zhu Peide, Ma Fuxiang, and others were present. Foreign guests included the ambassadors of Germany, Portugal, Spain, and Czechoslovakia, representatives of England, the United States, France, and Italy, and Japanese Consul-General Kamiya. Chiang Kai-shek, accompanied by his wife Soong Mei-ling, arrived at the airfield at 9:50 a.m. The military band played loudly, and they ascended the reviewing stand. After the meeting began as scheduled, Commander Gu Zhutong reported on horseback the number of people inspected. Wang Shihe, holding the Commander-in-Chief's flag, led the way. Chairman Chiang, along with Zhu Peide, Chen Yi, He Yaozu, Zhou Yawei, Yang Jie, Wu Siyu, and others, held the military parade. Wherever Chairman Chiang passed, the soldiers saluted. After the review, they ascended the stand for the march-past. Each unit was led by a band, and the soldiers paid attention to the presidential stand. The marching was orderly and the spirit was invigorated. The troops reviewed included the 1st Division Infantry Regiment, the 2nd Division Infantry Regiment, a cavalry squadron, an artillery regiment, five tank platoons, and an engineer communications battalion from the Guards, totaling more than 10,000 people. Each regiment had a band platoon attached, a communications platoon, four automatic machine guns, and four mortars. At 10:00 a.m., the Aviation Administration sent six aircraft to soar through the sky, perform stunts, and parachute. After the review, Chairman Chiang delivered a speech, then called out slogans and adjourned the meeting.

Memorial Meeting of the Central Party Headquarters The Central Party Headquarters held a National Day memorial meeting yesterday morning at 8:00 a.m. More than 600 people attended, including Chiang Kai-shek, Dai Chuanxian, Ding Weifen, Fang Juehui, Wang Boqun, Shao Lizi, Soong Ziwen, Chen Guofu, Chen Lifu, Enhe Batu, Zhou Qigang, Zhang Daofan, Shao Yuanchong, and Kong Xiangxi. After the ceremony, Ding Weifen presided, and Dai Chuanxian gave a report, stating that the Republic of China had been born for twenty years, which, according to individuals, was the age of coming of age. It should be well constructed, but it has not yet reached the point of being an independent and free person. The people are very distressed. This year's National Day is being spent in the midst of national crisis. Our party feels an even greater responsibility and the work is even more arduous. From today onwards, everyone should be determined to be loyal to the country and filial to the nation, throw away the calculation of personal gain and focus on the task at hand. Only then can the national crisis be safely overcome and the future will still be bright. The more dangerous the situation, the more important order becomes, and the more important individual duties become. When disaster strikes, civil officials can live and die with the local people, and soldiers can live and die with their weapons. The national crisis can certainly be overcome and final victory can be achieved. Therefore, the most important thing now is to unite as one. This is the determination that everyone should have today, he said. Then the ceremony was completed and the meeting adjourned.

Memorial Meeting of the Municipal Party Headquarters The Beijing Municipal Party Headquarters convened representatives from all walks of life yesterday morning at 10:00 a.m. in the auditorium to hold a National Day memorial meeting. More than 400 people attended. Chairman Lai Lian delivered a speech, stating that this year's National Day is being spent in the midst of national crisis, and who is not saddened? We commemorate National Day and vow to wipe out the humiliation. We must constantly struggle. If we want to survive, we must overthrow Japanese imperialism. Then, Liu Manpo, a representative of the Northeast Anti-Japanese Association who had fled to Beijing, was introduced to report on the atrocities of the Japanese army. Then Lou Tongsun and others gave speeches. Then the ceremony was completed and the meeting adjourned.

Wuhu National Day National Salvation Conference 86

Wuhu Correspondence: The water level in Wuhu city and rural areas is gradually receding, and the anti-Japanese national salvation movement is rising day by day. The Party Headquarters has convened meetings of all sectors to organize the Wuhu All Sectors Anti-Japanese National Salvation Volunteer Army Committee. The original organizations of agriculture, industry, commerce, and students have been unified and merged, and it is scheduled to be officially established on the 12th. Propaganda teams from various schools have been dispatched to the city and suburbs for days, shouting themselves hoarse. When workers, peasants, and women hear about it, they all weep. Many have voluntarily organized frugal groups and ten-person national salvation groups to prepare for national salvation. Not buying Japanese goods has become a unanimous action. Japanese ships recently passing through Wuhu have no passengers or goods embarking or disembarking, and they come and go quietly. Today is the National Day of Double Ten, and all sectors have suspended celebrations due to the ongoing national crisis, and only hang flags and close businesses to express national mourning. In order to arouse the public to jointly go to the national crisis, the county party headquarters specially held the Wuhu All Sectors Double Ten Anti-Japanese National Salvation Conference at the sports field of the East Gate Vocational and Commercial School at 9:00 a.m. More than 30,000 people from all sectors of the public and school boy scouts attended, and there was almost no room to stand in the meeting place. First, the chairman reported on the significance of the meeting, and then the draft telegram of the meeting was read out and passed by the whole body. Then representatives of various groups took the stage one after another to speak and then dispersed. (10th)

Local Correspondence Songjiang 87

The Anti-Japanese Association Identifies Enemy Goods The Anti-Japanese National Salvation Committee of this county has continuously inspected packages sent from Shanghai to Songjiang by postal mail at the transportation company, and found many pieces of suspected enemy goods such as undershirts and medicinal materials. The association had no way to judge, so Chang Mengxing and other members of the standing committee went to Shanghai to ask Ju Jiqiu, who had experience in identification from the Shanghai Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association, to come to Songjiang. Today (11th), they publicly inspected them one by one at the county party headquarters. Packages from Yuan Da Xin Ji and other three companies had one package of phonograph and more than ten pieces of unmarked cloth, which were quite suspicious. It was agreed that each piece should be cut off at the corner and taken to Shanghai for identification before further handling.

Wuxi 88

A Reward for Arresting Bandits Captured in Shanghai The vanguard officer Wang Yunlong of the 6th Team of the 2nd District of the Provincial Public Security Team stationed on the water in Wuxi received a confidential report the other day, stating that the bandit Zhou Changhai and his accomplice Fang Yiming were now fleeing to Shanghai. He requested that a team be sent to arrest them, and volunteered to lead the arrest. Upon receiving the report, Vanguard Officer Wang immediately took the team members and informants by car to Shanghai, and together with detectives from the British Concession police station, arrested the two bandits in Room 24 of the Ruizhong Hotel and escorted them to the police station. He then returned to Wuxi to report to the district office, and it was decided that they would take a document to Shanghai today (12th) to welcome them back and bring them to justice for interrogation. In addition, the bandit Zhou Changhai had been wanted by the county government of this county with a reward of 300 yuan.

Changzhou 89

Burning Two Batches of Enemy Goods The Inspection Section of the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association of Wujin recently discovered a box of enemy goods such as porcelain and glassware, and also discovered eleven packages of Xiantao brand enemy yarn. At 10:00 a.m. on the Double Ten Festival, people from all walks of life were summoned to burn them at the public sports field. The porcelain and other items were also smashed. At that time, propaganda teams from various schools gave speeches on the spot, and everyone was moved.

Zhenjiang 90

Misunderstanding Between Students and the Chamber of Commerce The other day, the Anti-Japanese Association unfortunately had a dispute with the Chamber of Commerce due to the work of inspecting goods, as seen in yesterday's newspaper. Yesterday morning around 8:00 a.m., the provincial government summoned Lu Xiaobo, the chairman of the Chamber of Commerce, to the government by telephone to discuss the matter. Chairman Ye instructed him in person that in this time of trouble, merchants must operate their businesses with peace of mind and must not take any action that would cause accidents. Lu agreed to take full responsibility. After returning to the association, he convened a temporary meeting to report on the situation. After the meeting dispersed, at 1:30 p.m., male and female students from various schools lined up to shout slogans on South Ma Road until they reached the gate of the Chamber of Commerce. They unanimously demanded that Chairman Lu answer on the spot the meaning of yesterday's goods lifting. At this time, Chairman Lu was not in the association, and no one came forward. While they were in a stalemate, Standing Committee Member Hu Jianchun came to the association from outside. Many representatives ordered him to answer, but Hu said that he had not attended every meeting and replied that he was completely unaware of the situation. During the misunderstanding of words, it was inevitable that there were many people and hands, and Hu's face was slightly injured, and a piece of Hu's azure silk vest was torn. Then the provincial government persuaded the students to return first, and Hu went to the provincial party headquarters to resolve the matter together. The students from various schools then lined up and returned to school along West Gate Avenue. Hu immediately followed the provincial government's car to the provincial party headquarters to resolve everything. In the evening, Chairman Ye of the provincial government convened both parties to a meeting in the province. After discussion, one party restrained the merchants and the other party persuaded the students not to expand the situation again. It is said that Hu Jianchun entered Hongren Hospital yesterday.

Nantong 91

The Embezzlement Case of Burning Opium Still Has No Clue The Nantong County Court burned opium and discovered that more than 1,000 taels of opium had been embezzled. The Procuratorate, upon the order of the High Court, summoned the people involved in the case for investigation. They all shirked responsibility to each other. Wu Pingzhang, the clerk, was released on bail and has now recorded his statement and submitted it to the High Court for review and handling.

Anti-Japanese Association Sets Up Wooden Cages The Nantong Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association has set up wooden cages at the gates of the city for the purpose of having treacherous merchants and corrupt officials within the association stand in them when they are caught.

Hangzhou 92

A Large Batch of Japanese Goods Seized and Confiscated The Hangzhou Anti-Japanese National Salvation Federation received a confidential report yesterday that the Meiheng Soap Factory under the Guojun Bridge River was privately selling a large batch of Japanese goods. It secretly dispatched inspectors to investigate and found 80 baskets of the Japanese raw material called "hardened material" used to manufacture soap, worth more than 4,000 yuan. The factory was posing as butter to deceive and did not register or seal them. The Japanese goods were immediately taken to the association and confiscated in full. In addition, inspectors from the association checked the two refrigerators purchased by the Hangzhou Power Plant from Shanghai at the Zhakou, and they seemed to be Japanese goods. They were immediately detained pending a thorough investigation before disposal.

Pinghu 93

Treacherous Merchants Discovered Shipping Japanese Goods by Mail Since the Japanese army invaded the East, the treacherous merchants of this city have considered it a great opportunity and secretly purchased a large batch of Japanese goods from Shanghai for delivery by post, which has happened more than once. Yesterday, the Hengtai Xiang, Yuanchang Xiang, and Daheng silk and satin shops also imported more than 30 pieces of Japanese silk, which were still transshipped from Jiaxing. They were discovered and detained by the Jiaxing Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association, which telegraphed the Pinghu Anti-Japanese Association to send personnel to the post office to receive them and punish the treacherous merchants according to law.

Troops Deployed to Zhapu Zhang Nanxian, Chairman of the Provincial Government, believes that the coastal and land defenses of the entire province are important due to the current invasion of our territory by the violent Japanese. He has transferred the 2nd and 3rd Battalions of the 7th Regiment of the Provincial Security Team to Zhapu to guard the coast to prevent Japanese warships from invading. He also ordered County Magistrate Wu to supervise the military and police to strictly guard against the winter defense period being handled earlier.

Xiaoshan 94

Military Training for Party and Government Personnel The Xiaoshan Party and government authorities began military training for all affiliated agencies starting on the 9th. Employees of party and government agencies enthusiastically signed up. Those aged between 20 and 40 joined together in accordance with provincial orders. Except for those with special official business and serious illnesses, no one was allowed to ask for leave.

Entertainment Suspended Amid National Crisis

Prior to the meeting, the municipal party headquarters notified all sectors to participate and notified all sectors to suspend all entertainment. The details of the meeting are supplemented as follows:

Meeting Order (1) Music; (2) All Stand 96

Up; (3) Sing the Party Song; (4) Pay the Highest Respects to the Party Flag, National Flag, and the Portrait of the Premier; (5) The Chairman Respectfully Reads the Premier's Last Will; (6) Silent Tribute; (7) Chairman's Report; (8) Speeches; (9) Shout Slogans; (10) Adjournment

Participating Groups Municipal Party 97

Headquarters, Municipal Government, Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, Municipal Education Bureau, Municipal Health Bureau, Municipal Public Security Bureau, Municipal Public Utilities Bureau, Municipal Public Works Bureau, Garrison Headquarters, College of Political Science and Law, Jiaotong University, Cultural College, Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association, Women's Relief Association, Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Citizens' Federation, Law School, National Goods Market, Party Headquarters of Districts 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6, 7, 8, 9, and 10, Directly Subordinate Branches, Branches in Various Districts of This City, Postal Workers' Union, Representatives of Various Primary and Secondary Schools, Various Agencies, Various Labor Unions, etc., approximately 1,000 people

Meeting Staff Presidium Tao Baichuan, Wang 98

Xiaolai, Chen Kecheng, Zhu Yingpeng, Fu Dewei, Jiang Yi, Zhu Youhuan, Recorder Zhou Hanmei, Master of Ceremonies Xu Yefu, Reception Fang Weiren, Wang Xuequan

Chairman's Report Wang Xiaolai delivered the opening address, 99

saying, "Gentlemen, today is the National Day memorial meeting for the 20th year of the Republic of China. When we think of the dangerous national status and the shaking national foundation of the Republic of China in its 20th year, and the urgency of internal and external troubles, not only is there no celebration to be had, but it is simply heartbreaking. Tears stream down our faces. Floods have reached sixteen provinces, affecting 60 to 70 million victims. Isn't this a huge internal trouble? Japanese imperialism has launched a large-scale invasion and occupation of the Eastern Provinces, losing thousands of miles of territory. The loss of people's lives and property is incalculable. Isn't this a huge external trouble? Therefore, today's National Day memorial is not a celebration, but only a lament. We cannot be sad, only strive. From today onwards, all citizens should take on two very important responsibilities. The first is that everyone should be of one mind and one heart to save the flood victims. The second is that all people should resist foreign insults with one heart. We sacrifice our lives, property, and energy to strive to complete these two major tasks, spraying our hot blood and heads and nailing them to these two heavy crucifixes. In previous National Days, we were always grand and joyful. This year's National Day is simply bleak, tragic, and extremely desolate. Compatriots, can you no longer wake up? Let us all loudly shout two slogans: first, unanimously strive to relieve the flood victims; second, unanimously strive to resist foreign insults. Otherwise, the suffering of the people of the Three Northeastern Provinces will immediately make the 400 million people of the whole country taste the suffering of national subjugation. The life of the nation and the glory of the country are all on our shoulders. We hope that everyone will rise up together. That's all."

Meeting Slogans (1) Commemorate National Day to Uphold 100

Peace and Unity; (2) Commemorate National Day, Do Not Forget National Crisis; (3) Commemorate National Day, Do Not Forget the Flood Victims; (4) Commemorate National Day, Resist Foreign Insults; (5) Drive the Japanese Soldiers Out of the Country; (6) Permanently Sever Economic Relations with Japan; (7) Down with Japanese Imperialism; (8) Long Live the Republic of China; (9) Long Live the Chinese Kuomintang

Chen Mingshu Returned to Shanghai Yesterday 104

Gu Mengyu and Huang Huabiao Accompanied Him

Took the Train to Beijing Last Night to Report His Mission

National Peace Is Expected to Be Realized

Wang, Sun, and Li are Waiting for Hu's Telegram in Guangzhou

Central Executive Committee member Chen Mingshu, accompanied by Central Supervisory Committee members Cai Yuanpei and Zhang Ji, went to Guangzhou with the Central Government's mission to negotiate peace. Yesterday afternoon at 3:00 p.m., Chen returned to Shanghai aboard the British ship "Gelifen." Accompanying him were Guangdong representative Gu Mengyu and his wife, Guangxi representative Huang Huabiao, and Chen's adjutants Pang Fei and Liu Shumo, a party of five. The detailed situation is described as follows:

Met a Storm En Route Chen and others took the British ship to Shanghai from Hong Kong on the 7th. It was rumored that they took the Dutch ship "Hualizhi Wang," which was not true. Although the Dutch ship sailed from Hong Kong on the same day, it will not arrive until this morning. The British ship "Gelifen" was originally scheduled to arrive in Shanghai at noon the other day, but was delayed for a day due to a hurricane encountered en route. Yesterday afternoon at 1:00 p.m., the ship arrived at Wusong. At 2:30 p.m., it docked at the Pudong Wharf in Yangshupu.

Welcome at the Wharf Yesterday, Mayor Zhang Qun, Central Executive Committee member Wu Tiecheng, and Jiang Haiguan Supervisor Tang Haian, representing Soong Ziwen, and Vice Commander Zhang's representative Luo Wengan and more than a dozen others took a specially prepared public safety launch from the new customs wharf across the river to board the ship to welcome them. At about 3:00 p.m., the welcoming party accompanied Chen and others back to the new customs wharf and took a car to the Cangzhou Hotel. Gu and Huang stayed at a friend's place.

Made a Statement Chen made a special statement yesterday, saying, "Question: Mr., what is the effect of your visit to Guangdong to discuss peace? Answer: Faced with national crisis, comrades from all parties in our party must unite in spirit and urgently seek peaceful unification. I am conveying the sincere intention of both parties to the same request, and I am not acting as a peace envoy. Question: Can peaceful unification be realized? Answer: The people of the whole country can consciously resist foreign enemies and yearn for peaceful unification. The Kuomintang is a party that should follow the trend and appeal to the people. How can it violate public sentiment? Since public sentiment is becoming unanimous, it will certainly succeed. Question: What method will be used to promote its realization? Answer: After I report my mission to Beijing, Mr. Chiang and Mr. Hu and others will schedule an appointment with comrades in Guangdong to meet in Shanghai with the two comrades Cai and Zhang, waiting for the Guangdong comrades to come. When the meeting is held, it will be the time when peaceful unification is realized. Question: When will you take up the post of garrison commander in Beijing and Shanghai? Answer: Not yet decided. When I take up this post, I must first resign from the Central Political Conference Committee and the National Government Committee. It is not appropriate to participate in national affairs while wholeheartedly guarding the central government, so as to avoid the suspicion of the military interfering in politics. It is also in line with my long-standing proposition of not holding military and political posts concurrently."

Meeting at Zhang's Residence Yesterday afternoon at 3:30 p.m., Central Executive Committee members Wu Zhihui, Li Shizeng, Wu Tiecheng, Zhang Qun, Zhang Jingjiang, and Chen Mingshu met at Zhang Jingjiang's residence on Masnan Road. Chen reported on the trip and discussed cooperation methods. They dispersed after two hours. Chu Minyi went to Zhang's residence once during the meeting, but soon left.

Wu Tiecheng's Talk Mr. Wu Tiecheng told our reporter yesterday that the peaceful unification of the country is extremely optimistic. Chen and others will take the train to Beijing tonight to report their mission. Mr. Hu will be able to come to Shanghai. After Hu arrives in Shanghai, the Guangdong comrades will send Wang Jingwei, Sun Ke, and Li Wenfan to Shanghai to meet. The meeting place has not been decided in Beijing and Shanghai. It is generally more likely to be in Shanghai. The two comrades Cai and Zhang will come with Wang and others at that time.

Li Shizeng's Talk When the reporter met Mr. Li Shizeng yesterday, he said that Mr. Gu Mengyu is currently staying in Shanghai temporarily, waiting for the three comrades Wang, Sun, and Li to come to Shanghai. As for Mr. Hu's departure from Beijing to Shanghai, it is certainly not a problem. The detailed method will be determined after consultation with Chairman Chiang in Beijing.

Gu Mengyu's Talk Mr. Gu Mengyu told reporters yesterday that the public sentiment in Hong Kong and Guangdong is extremely agitated, and the hope for peaceful unification is particularly urgent. I came to Shanghai due to private friendship, not as a formal representative of Guangdong. The Guangdong side did not propose conditions, but a method. Now the Beijing side has Chen Mingshu in charge of guarding Beijing and Shanghai, and has allowed Mr. Hu to leave Beijing to come to Shanghai. Therefore, the Guangdong comrades have agreed to come to Shanghai for consultation. As for the personal issue of staying or leaving, it will be resolved publicly in the meeting. The rumors of assigning party, military, and political work are absolutely not true. After all, the government is a whole, how can it be forcibly divided? If that is the case, it is actually close to spoils sharing.

Left for Beijing Last Night Chen Mingshu, accompanied by Li Shizeng, Wu Zhihui, Wu Tiecheng, Zhang Jingjiang, Xiong Shihui, Luo Wengan, and Chen's secretary Sun Xiwu, took the night express to Beijing at 11:00 p.m. last night to meet with Chairman Chiang and report on the negotiations. The North Railway Station was temporarily under martial law last night, and the security was extremely tight.

Yesterday's Memorial of the Premier's Martyrdom 105

People from All Walks of Life Held a Meeting at the Municipal Party Headquarters

Yesterday was the 35th anniversary of the Premier's martyrdom in London. The Shanghai Special Municipal Party Headquarters specially convened representatives from all walks of life to hold a memorial meeting in the Grand Auditorium on the third floor of the Shanghai Municipal Party Headquarters. By the time the meeting began, more than 500 representatives from various agencies, groups, and schools in the city had arrived. Chairman Pan Gongzhan presided over the meeting. First, the chairman gave a report, followed by speeches by Chen Kecheng and others. The ceremony was completed and the meeting adjourned.

Japanese Residents in Shanghai Provoke 106

Following Yesterday's Residents' General Meeting

Forcibly Tear Down Slogans

Wanton Abuse

Kick and Injure Chinese

Japanese residents in Shanghai held a general meeting at the Japanese Elementary School on North Sichuan Road at 1 PM yesterday to discuss how to counter our country's anti-Japanese national salvation movement. After the meeting, several hundred Japanese marched south along North Sichuan Road, forcibly tearing down patriotic slogans posted by various shops, provoking incidents in every possible way. Japanese Marines specially dispatched armed soldiers in military vehicles, following behind the Japanese who were causing trouble, demonstrating along the road. For a time, the situation was tense and order was disrupted along North Sichuan Road from Yokohama Bridge to Pengpu Road. Shops closed their doors one after another to temporarily avoid their aggression. The details are as follows:

Forcibly Tearing Down Slogans The location where the Japanese held their meeting was the Northern Japanese Elementary School at No. 141 North Sichuan Road, north of Yokohama Bridge. From noon yesterday, a large number of Japanese Marines, armed with guns and live ammunition, were stationed along the road. Except for Japanese attendees, Chinese were unable to pass. The meeting began around 3 PM and concluded. Then, three to four hundred Japanese attendees formed small groups and headed south, forcibly tearing down patriotic slogans posted by Chinese shops along the roadside, regardless of reason, and wantonly abusing them verbally, making it impossible to reason with them.

Deliberately Provoking Incidents Starting from Yokohama Bridge, many Chinese shops along the way were harassed by the Japanese. The large group suddenly stopped in front of the Jiande Apartment at No. 713. Immediately, several Japanese thugs climbed onto the copper railings outside the glass window and tore down the large-character banner "Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association Propaganda Team Stationed Here" and various slogans posted on it. Hundreds of Japanese onlookers clapped and cheered.

Shops Close Their Doors Taking advantage of the situation, the Japanese marched towards Bazili Road. When they reached the southern end of Qiujiang Road, they invaded the Lianchang Hardware Store at No. 516 again, tearing down slogans and harassing them in every possible way. At this time, shops closed their doors one after another to avoid their aggression and temporarily suspended business. However, over a hundred Japanese swaggered south from Bazili Road.

Kicking and Injuring Shop Assistants When they arrived at the Wang Shengtie Western Clothing Store near Pengpu Road, the store was preparing to close its iron gate. The Japanese, regardless of everything, forcibly tried to tear down the slogans pasted inside the glass window. Wang Huihua, the small shop owner, was unable to stop them and was kicked in the lower abdomen. Wang Xianqing's left hand was also struck, causing a lot of bleeding. They were both examined by a Western doctor, and a letter was sent to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, the Taxpaying Chinese Association, the Citizens' Federation, and the Anti-Japanese Association, urging them to actively negotiate.

Armed Demonstration When the Japanese were tearing down slogans in groups, armed Marines in military vehicles provided cover behind them and demonstrated along the way. The concession police also dispatched detectives to disperse the Japanese and maintain order when they caused trouble.

Extreme Prevention On both sides of North Sichuan Road, the area belongs to the Chinese territory. When something happened, the heads of the fifth district, the first branch of the fifth district, and the second branch of the fifth district of the Public Security Bureau warned the police to take extreme precautions and, after the incident, persuaded the shops to open their doors and restore the original state. Chen Xizeng, the head of the Public Security Bureau, also went to Zhabei to investigate the truth after receiving the news and will submit a request to the municipal government to protest to the Japanese consulate.

What Was Heard at the Meeting It was heard that the Japanese residents' general meeting yesterday was attended by store owners and employees of various Japanese shops, heads of various households, and consular military and police officials, totaling more than 7,000 people. The venue was heavily guarded. The most important resolution was to send a telegram to the Tokyo government, stating that the lives and property of residents in Shanghai are in imminent danger, and requesting that decisive action be taken against the anti-Japanese national salvation movement in China. It was also said that after the meeting, the Japanese, because our country's anti-Japanese national salvation movement has been strictly maintaining order and there is no opportunity to take advantage of, and because they are feeling the impact of the major boycott of Japanese goods, had no choice but to deliberately provoke incidents to find an excuse, hence the action of marching in groups and forcibly tearing down slogans.

Two Japanese Warships Have Arrived in Shanghai 107

More Than 200 Marines Have Landed

The Tenryū and Tokiwa, two Japanese warships that arrived in Shanghai the day before yesterday, are now anchored in the river at Yangshupu. Of the 400 Marines brought by the Tokiwa, 240 landed at Huishan Wharf at around 4 PM on the day of arrival and took cars to the barracks in front of Hongkou Park at the end of North Sichuan Road. The Japanese side stated that this was to protect the僑民 (overseas residents) in the Hongkou area. The rest remain on the ship.

What Was Heard Yesterday About the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Movement 108

The Anti-Japanese Conference Resolved Many Important Cases

The Anti-Japanese Association's Fifth Executive Committee Meeting

Refuse to Load Foreign Goods on Japanese Ships Coming to China

Relief for Unemployed Seamen from Japanese Factories

Stop Unscrupulous Merchants from Hoarding and Raising Prices

Recruit Overseas Chinese Merchants to Return to the Country and Establish Factories

Passed Two Training Outlines for Volunteer Army

The Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association held its fifth executive committee meeting yesterday, electing Lu Jingshi as chairman and Feng Yixian and Zhao Shusheng as recorders. (1) Discussed the case of how to handle the Shanghai Universities Anti-Japanese National Salvation Federation's request to immediately convene anti-Japanese national salvation groups to hold a joint meeting. Resolved: the Standing Committee will convene a discussion. (2) Discussed the organization of the Shanghai Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association Volunteer Army Finance Committee and the economic independence case. Resolved: approved in principle, Wang Hanmin, Xi Yushu, and Xie Fusheng were appointed as three committee members to draft the articles of association, and Wang Hanliang was designated as the convener. (3) The Design Committee suggested that the inspection offices in each district implement concrete measures to inspect Japanese goods in each store. Resolved: (A) Personnel from the inspection offices in each district should inspect Japanese goods in each store in conjunction with personnel from the Japanese goods inspection group of each trade association. (B) Trade associations that have already established Japanese goods inspection groups should register with the Inspection Department of this association within seven days. (C) Trade associations that have not established Japanese goods inspection groups must establish them within seven days and register with the Inspection Department of this association. (D) If a trade association still fails to establish a Japanese goods inspection group after the deadline, the inspection offices in each district of this association may send personnel to inspect independently. (E) If disputes arise between inspectors of this association and inspectors of each trade association due to the identification of Japanese goods, if the chairman of each trade association or more than three standing committee members provide a written certificate proving that the goods are definitely not Japanese goods, they may be temporarily allowed not to be detained and sealed in the original place. This association will then take samples and ask experts to review them. If it is found to be Japanese goods, the chairman of each trade association or more than three standing committee members should be held jointly responsible with the owner. (4) How to provide relief to employees who withdraw from companies, foreign firms, banks, shipping companies, and factories operated by Japanese merchants. Resolved: (1) (Spinning mill workers) The committee members are responsible for contacting the Chinese Spinning Mill Federation to arrange placement, and please ask each factory to add cloth machines. (2) (Bank personnel) Because the number of people is small, a letter must be sent to Chinese banks to find a way to arrange placement, which should not be a problem. (3) (Foreign firm personnel) After Japanese goods become sluggish, Western goods will definitely flourish, and the number of Western firm employees should be increased. Please ask the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to find a way to introduce them. (4) (Seamen) You can directly send letters to the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, the Sanbei Steamship Company, and the Shipping Association. The number of shipping routes and ships must be increased. (5) (Miscellaneous factory workers) Please ask the four national goods groups to try their best to accommodate them. (6) (Dock workers) Distribute them to various docks as much as possible. (3) How to stop the price increase of domestic goods. Resolved: This association will publish a warning in the newspaper. If there are unscrupulous merchants who deliberately hoard goods, they will be punished for disrupting economic sanctions against Japan. The Investigation Department of this association will also study the needs and supply of various goods at any time to prevent unscrupulous merchants from raising prices under the pretext of shortage. (5) Recruiting overseas Chinese to return to the country and establish factories to permanently boycott Japanese goods. Resolved: This association will send a telegram to overseas Chinese chambers of commerce. (6) How to avoid loading foreign orders on Japanese ships. Resolved: (1) This association will forward a letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to inform the International Chamber of Commerce that if goods arriving in China in the future are loaded on Japanese ships or if ships arriving in China dock at Japanese wharves, loading and unloading will inevitably be difficult. Please pay close attention. (2) Letters to all Chinese merchants stipulate in the contracts signed with foreign merchants that all new goods must not be loaded on Japanese ships; otherwise, the goods will be returned and all losses will be compensated. (7) How to dispose of confiscated Japanese goods. Resolved: Xi Yushu, Zhang Zilian, Xie Fusheng, Li Cishan, and Li Wenlie were appointed as five committee members to formulate concrete measures for further discussion and designated Li Wenlie as the convener. (9) Discussed the reconsideration of the Yuanlaihang tapioca flour case. Resolved: Shi Liangcai, Wang Changyuan, Hu Shuhua, Ren Jinpin, Xu Mojue, Zhang Ziwei, Wang Pingnan, Long Peiyun, and Lu Muqin were appointed as nine committee members to review it. (10) Discussed the compilation and training plan outline for the group volunteer army. Resolved: passed.

Outline for Primary Officer Training (1) Establish a primary officer training school to specialize in training primary officers of this army. (2) The first primary officer training will be for 100 people, and the second training will be for 200 people, to be used to fill the primary officer positions of the three divisions. (3) Candidates for primary officers will be selected from two aspects: (A) Members of the defense group, (B) Soldiers who have registered this time. (4) Members of the defense group and registered soldiers who meet the following qualifications will be admitted to the training school: (A) Aged between 20 and 30, (B) Not responsible for family life, (C) Having received military training for more than two years, (D) Physically fit and able to endure hardship, (E) During the training period, the first session is one week, and the second session is one month. Those who score excellent or above in the examination will be included in the first training session. (F) All trainees will be enlisted, provided with food and accommodation. (G) The training will be temporarily divided into four subjects: infantry, artillery, engineering, and logistics. The training subjects for each subject will be determined separately. (H) The training school should find ways to prepare sufficient military equipment for application. (I) The operating expenses will be budgeted separately, with a total amount tentatively set at 13,000 yuan. (J) Guns will be temporarily borrowed from the defense group, and artillery will be borrowed from the army when experiments are needed. (K) Instructors for the training school will be appointed by the Training Directorate or the Garrison Headquarters.

Organization of Group Volunteer Army (1) All groups, companies, factories, etc. that voluntarily organize volunteer armies shall be subject to this plan. (2) All those who organize volunteer armies must have at least 33 or more people. (3) All soldiers who join the volunteer army must pass the examination by the personnel sent by this association. (4) The numbers shall be uniformly compiled by this association. Those with a full 33 people shall be listed as one platoon, those with three full platoons shall be listed as one company, those with three full companies shall be listed as one battalion, and those with three full battalions shall be listed as one regiment. (5) The peacetime organization of the group volunteer army shall be based on battalions. Those who do not have a full battalion shall merge with other groups nearby to form a battalion. (6) The officers of the group volunteer army shall be selected and dispatched by this association. When each group has suitable talents, they may be responsible for recommending them, but they must be reviewed and qualified by this association before being appointed. (7) All soldiers who join this army must receive at least two hours of unified training every day. When necessary, the time may be increased. (8) After employees of each company, store, or factory join this army, this association will notify the owners of each factory and store, and each soldier will be allowed two hours for training time, without deducting wages. If the training time needs to be increased, it will be handled in the same way. (9) The clothing of each soldier and officer shall be in accordance with the style stipulated by this association and shall be provided by the group or soldier. (10) The training location and time shall be designated by this association. (11) If each group can prepare its own military equipment, it shall be responsible for its safekeeping. If it cannot prepare its own military equipment, it shall be temporarily issued and used by this association during training, and shall be returned to this association for storage after use. (12) The method of temporary assembly shall be determined by this association at any time. (13) The group volunteer army must absolutely obey military discipline. (14) If there are any matters not covered, this committee shall revise them at any time.

National Salvation Volunteer Army 109

The First Regiment's Organization Is Ready

Speeches Were Given Yesterday at the Public Sports Ground

According to 국민社 (National Society), the National Salvation Volunteer Army Committee, sponsored by the Shanghai Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association, gave speeches at the Public Sports Ground to more than 1,000 volunteer soldiers of the First Regiment that has been organized. Prior to this, the committee appointed Zhou Yanan as the commander of the regiment, Deng Jinglie, Huang Dapeng, Zheng Xingli, Xu Tao, Cheng Xiuyan, Sheng Duhu, Peng Yangwu, Mo Caiwen, Li Shuming, Chu Jinming, Yang Yinmin, and Wu Yan as squadron leaders. Committee members Chen Yafu and Li Cishan gave training, briefly stating, "Comrades, today is the first time that the Shanghai National Salvation Volunteer Army Committee has organized a large gathering of soldiers who are willing to sacrifice themselves for the country after being organized by the Compilation Office. It is also the day when training will begin for future combat. At this time when the situation and environment are precarious, comrades, you have enthusiastically come to gather here early in the morning. This spirit is gratifying. The Japanese are taking advantage of our China's natural and man-made disasters with an aggressive Manchurian-Mongolian policy, using troops to invade and occupy the three northeastern provinces without any conscience, seizing land, burning cities, killing and capturing people, doing what humans are unwilling to do. After this unfortunate news came, the people of the whole country, no matter who they were, embraced infinite grief and were extremely willing to fight the Japanese to the death. This time, the troops in the three northeastern provinces surrendered the great territory to the Japanese without resistance, which made our people even more grieved and humiliated. The Chinese people's weakness is so obvious that it makes us weep bitterly. We are now organizing a volunteer army. This organization is the strength of the people. With the strength of an entire people, we can go to the national crisis together and save the country with all our strength. The mission and responsibility of each volunteer soldier is very important. We should shoulder this great mission and responsibility of saving the country, saving the nation, and saving ourselves. Once we have shouldered it on our shoulders, we will not fear anything, sacrifice ourselves desperately, and absolutely not shrink back or be afraid of death. In short, we must love our motherland. We must resist with the strength of the entire nation, the entire organized and trained force. It is not enough to save this critical situation. Not only must we expel the Japanese troops from the three northeastern provinces and return our territory, but we must also take on all the great missions and responsibilities of the future with a persistent spirit," and so on. Next, Committee member Li Cishan and others gave training, and then the team was organized and dismissed. It is heard that the association is now planning to compile the unorganized volunteer soldiers into the second, third, and other regiments. It has been decided that the first regiment, which has been fully compiled, will begin training on the 15th of this month.
